class="wrap"><div id="primary" class="content-area"><main id="main" class="site-main" role="main"><section id="" class="py-5"  ><div class="container"><div class="row justify-content-lg-center"><div class=" col-12 col-lg-10"><div class="custom"><h2 class="title display-4">Updates Regarding VSA Security Incident</h2></div></div><div class=" col-12 col-lg-10"><div class="custom"><h3 class="subtitle h3">July 26, 2021 - 1:00 PM EDT</h3><div class="description"><p>Throughout this past weekend, Kaseyas Incident Response team and Emsisoft partners continued their work assisting our customers and others with restoration of their encrypted data.  We continue to provide the decryptor to customers that request it, and we encourage all our customers whose data may have been encrypted during the attack to reach out to your contacts at Kaseya.  The decryption tool has proven 100% effective at decrypting files that were fully encrypted in the attack.</p><p>Kaseya has maintained our focus on assisting our customers, and when Kaseya obtained the decryptor last week we moved as quickly as possible to safely use the decryptor to help our customers recover their encrypted data. Recent reports have suggested that our continued silence on whether Kaseya paid the ransom may encourage additional ransomware attacks, but nothing could be further from our goal.  While each company must make its own decision on whether to pay the ransom, Kaseya decided after consultation with experts to not negotiate with the criminals who perpetrated this attack and we have not wavered from that commitment.  As such, we are confirming in no uncertain terms that Kaseya did not pay a ransom  either directly or indirectly through a third party  to obtain the decryptor.</p><p>&nbsp;</p></div><h3 class="subtitle h3">July 23, 2021 - 3:00 PM EDT</h3><div class="description"><p>Kaseya&#8217;s Incident Response team, assisted by Emsisoft, continues to provide our customers with the decryption key and help them to restore any encrypted data that was not previously restored from backup. We have no reports of problems or issues with the decryptor.</p><p>&nbsp;</p></div><h3 class="subtitle h3">July 22, 2021 - 3:30 PM EDT</h3><div class="description"><p><b>Kaseya has obtained universal decryptor key.</b></p><p>On 7/21/2021, Kaseya obtained a decryptor for victims of the REvil ransomware attack, and were working to remediate customers impacted by the incident.</p><p>We can confirm that Kaseya obtained the tool from a third party and have teams actively helping customers affected by the ransomware to restore their environments, with no reports of any problem or issues associated with the decryptor. Kaseya is working with <u><a title="https://www.emsisoft.com/" href="https://www.emsisoft.com/">Emsisoft</a></u> to support our customer engagement efforts, and Emsisoft has confirmed the key is effective at unlocking victims.</p><p>We remain committed to ensuring the highest levels of safety for our customers and will continue to update here as more details become available.</p><p>Customers who have been impacted by the ransomware will be contacted by Kaseya representatives.</p></div><h3 class="subtitle h3">July 19, 2021 - 3:15 PM EDT</h3><div class="description"><p><strong>VSA 9.5.7.3011 Maintenance Patch Release Update</strong></p><p>Kaseya is releasing patch 9.5.7.3011 which remediates functionality issues <u>caused by the enhanced security measures put in place</u> and provides bug fixes (this is not a security release). The full release notes with the fixes are available at: <u><a title="https://helpdesk.kaseya.com/hc/en-gb/articles/4404146456209" href="https://helpdesk.kaseya.com/hc/en-gb/articles/4404146456209">https://helpdesk.kaseya.com/hc/en-gb/articles/4404146456209</a></u>.</p><p><strong>VSA SaaS Update</strong></p><p>The first VSA SaaS deployment went live on Saturday July 17th US EDT for the following VSA SaaS instances: EU &#8211; SAAS03, EU &#8211; SAAS06, EU &#8211; SAAS11, EU &#8211; SAAS12, EU &#8211; SAAS16, EU &#8211; SAAS23, EU &#8211; SAAS24, EU &#8211; SAAS25, EU &#8211; SAAS28, EU &#8211; SAAS34, EU &#8211; SAAS39, EU &#8211; SAAS41 ,EU &#8211; SAAS43, US &#8211; NA1VSA01, US &#8211; NA1VSA04, US &#8211; NA1VSA08, US &#8211; NA1VSA12, US &#8211; NA1VSA14, US &#8211; NA1VSA22, US &#8211; NA1VSA28, US &#8211; NA1VSA29, US &#8211; NA1VSA30, US &#8211; NA1VSA32, US &#8211; NA1VSA37, NA1VSA105, US &#8211; NA1VSA108, US &#8211; NA1VSA115, US &#8211; IAD2VSA02, US &#8211; IAD2VSA04</p><p>The remainder of the VSA SaaS instances will be updated tonight (July 19th) 8PM and 4AM US EDT.</p><p><strong>VSA On-Premises Update:</strong></p><p>The VSA On-Premises Patch will be released to customers and posted to the download site by 4:30PM US EDT today.</p></div><h3 class="subtitle h3">July 16, 2021 - 7:00 PM EDT</h3><div class="description"><p><b>VSA 9.5.7.3011 Maintenance Patch Release Update</b></p><p>Kaseya will be releasing patch 9.5.7.3011 which remediates functionality issues <u>caused by the enhanced security measures put in place</u> and provides bug fixes (this is not a security release). (this is <b><u>not</u></b> a security release). The full release notes with the fixes are available at: <u><a title="https://helpdesk.kaseya.com/hc/en-gb/articles/4404146456209" href="https://helpdesk.kaseya.com/hc/en-gb/articles/4404146456209">https://helpdesk.kaseya.com/hc/en-gb/articles/4404146456209</a></u>.</p><p>The patch is planned to be available for VSA On-Premises customers by Monday July 19<sup>th</sup> end of day.</p><p>The first VSA SaaS deployment is planned for Saturday July 17<sup>th</sup> between 7AM and 11AM US EDT for the following VSA SaaS instances: EU &#8211; SAAS03, EU &#8211; SAAS06, EU &#8211; SAAS11, EU &#8211; SAAS12, EU &#8211; SAAS16, EU &#8211; SAAS23, EU &#8211; SAAS24, EU &#8211; SAAS25, EU &#8211; SAAS28, EU &#8211; SAAS34, EU &#8211; SAAS39, EU &#8211; SAAS41 ,EU &#8211; SAAS43, US &#8211; NA1VSA01, US &#8211; NA1VSA04, US &#8211; NA1VSA08, US &#8211; NA1VSA12, US &#8211; NA1VSA14, US &#8211; NA1VSA22, US &#8211; NA1VSA28, US &#8211; NA1VSA29, US &#8211; NA1VSA30, US &#8211; NA1VSA32, US &#8211; NA1VSA37, NA1VSA105, US &#8211; NA1VSA108, US &#8211; NA1VSA115, US &#8211; IAD2VSA02, US &#8211; IAD2VSA04</p><p>The remainder of the VSA SaaS instances are planned for deployment between 8PM and 4AM US EDT on Monday July 19<sup>th</sup>.</p></div><h3 class="subtitle h3">July 14, 2021 - 5:00 PM EDT</h3><div class="description"><p><b>VSA Install Patch Check</b></p><p>When running the Kinstall patch on your VSA, if you chose to reinstall VSA and either <b>unchecked</b> the default option to install the latest patch, or <b>reran</b> the Reinstall VSA process a 2<sup>nd</sup>time <b>without</b> the install patch option selected  its possible your patch was not re-applied.</p><p>While these are rare edge cases, we recommend that you verify that the latest patch was installed properly. We have made a tool that enables you to ensure the patch is properly install.</p><p>Download the verification tool at: <u><a title="https://app.box.com/s/5kqsbdj9aajezsc63jzaadpka5esk1v8" href="https://app.box.com/s/5kqsbdj9aajezsc63jzaadpka5esk1v8">https://app.box.com/s/5kqsbdj9aajezsc63jzaadpka5esk1v8</a></u></p></div><h3 class="subtitle h3">July 13, 2021 - 8:00 PM EDT</h3><div class="description"><div data-tid="messageBodyContainer"><div data-tid="messageBodyContent"><p><b>VSA Update:</b></p><div data-tid="messageBodyContainer"><div data-tid="messageBodyContent"><p>Version 9.5.7a was released to both VSA SaaS and On-Premises on Sunday July 11<sup>th</sup>.</p><p>Please ensure you have reviewed the release notes at: <u><a title="https://helpdesk.kaseya.com/hc/en-gb/articles/4403785889041" href="https://helpdesk.kaseya.com/hc/en-gb/articles/4403785889041">https://helpdesk.kaseya.com/hc/en-gb/articles/4403785889041</a></u></p><p>Additionally, we recommend reviewing the following documents:</p><p>VSA On-Premises Integration IP Whitelist &#8211; <u><a title="https://helpdesk.kaseya.com/hc/en-gb/articles/4403869952657" href="https://helpdesk.kaseya.com/hc/en-gb/articles/4403869952657">https://helpdesk.kaseya.com/hc/en-gb/articles/4403869952657</a></u></p><p>On Premises Startup Runbook (Updated July 11<sup>th</sup>  Updated Step 4) &#8211; <u><a title="https://helpdesk.kaseya.com/hc/en-gb/articles/4403709150993incident-response" href="https://helpdesk.kaseya.com/hc/en-gb/articles/4403709150993incident-response">https://helpdesk.kaseya.com/hc/en-gb/articles/4403709150993incident-response</a></u></p><p>VSA On-Premise Hardening and Practice Guide &#8211; <u><a title="https://helpdesk.kaseya.com/hc/en-gb/articles/4403760102417" href="https://helpdesk.kaseya.com/hc/en-gb/articles/4403760102417">https://helpdesk.kaseya.com/hc/en-gb/articles/4403760102417</a></u></p><p>VSA SaaS Startup Runbook &#8211; This plan will consist of the following stages:</p><ul><li>Communication of our phased recovery plan with SaaS customers first followed by on-premises customers.<ul><li>In the spirit of responsible disclosure, Kaseya will be publishing a summary of the attack and what we have done to mitigate it.</li><li>Some lightly-used legacy VSA functionality will be removed as part of this release out of an abundance of caution. A specific list of the functionality and its impact on VSA capabilities will be outlined in the release notes.</li><li>There will be new security measures implemented including enhanced security monitoring of our SaaS servers by FireEye and enablement of enhanced WAF capabilities.</li><li>We have successfully completed an external Vulnerability Scan, checked our SaaS Databases for Indicators of Compromise, and have had external security experts review our code to ensure a successful service restart.</li></ul></li></ul><ul><li>SaaS Restoration Timeline Updates<ul><li>Our executive committee will meet on July 5<sup>th</sup> at 5:00 AM UTC (12:00 AM EDT) to make a readiness decision on restarting SaaS within the following time windows:<ul><li>EU, UK, &amp; APAC Data Centers: July 5 &#8211; 9:00 AM UTC  1:00 PM UTC (4:00 AM EDT  8:00 AM EDT)</li><li>North American Data Centers: July 5 &#8211; 5:00 PM EDT  10:00 PM EDT</li></ul></li><li>These times/dates are subject to change and a status update will be posted on the website by 1:00 AM UTC as to whether we are adhering to the above schedule or not. If not, we will publish a revised schedule at that time.</li></ul></li></ul><ul><li>For our SaaS Users:<ul><li>We will bring our SaaS data centers back online on a one-by-one basis starting with our EU, UK and APAC data centers followed by our North American data centers.</li><li>We will be adding an additional layer of security to our SaaS infrastructure which will change the underlying IP addresses of our VSA servers.</li></ul></li></ul><ul><li>For our On-Premises Users<ul><li>We are currently building our on-premises release to make available to customers. We will begin the communication of the on-premises release process on July 5</li><li>We are working on a program to enable us to extend our new security measures to our on-premises customers. Most details for this will be available prior to the release of the on-premises patch.</li></ul></li></ul><p><strong><u>Continued Advisory</u></strong></p><ul><li>All on-premises VSA Servers should continue to remain offline until further instructions from Kaseya about when it is safe to restore operations. A patch will be required to be installed prior to restarting the VSA and a set of recommendations on how to increase security posture.</li><li><strong>We have been advised by our outside experts, thatcustomers whoexperienced ransomware andreceive communication from the attackersshouldnot click onanylinks&#8211;theymay be weaponized.</strong></li><li>The new Compromise Detection Tool can be download at the following link: <a href="https://kaseya.app.box.com/s/0ysvgss7w48nxh8k1xt7fqhbcjxhas40">VSA Detection Tools.zip | Powered by Box</a> This tool analyzes a system (either VSA server or managed endpoint) and determines whether any indicators of compromise (IoC) are present.</li></ul></div><h3 class="subtitle h3">July 4, 2021 - 10:00 AM EDT</h3><div class="description"><p><em>Next Update will be published July 4th in the early afternoon EDT</em></p><p>Kaseyas VSAproducthas unfortunatelybeenthe victim of a sophisticated cyberattack.Due to ourteamsfast response, we believe that this has been localized to a very small number of on-premisescustomersonly.<br /> This update provides further detail on the 1:30 PM EDT update. <u>The changes are underlined for clarity.</u></p><p><u>Our security, support communications, and customer teams continue to work around the clock in all geographies through the weekend to resolve the issue and restore our customers to service.</u></p><p>This update provides further detail on the July 3, 2021 7:30 PM EDT and 9:00 PM EDT updates. <u>The changes are underlined for clarity.</u></p><p><b><u>Continued Advisory</u></b></p><ul><li>Hosted VSA Servers will become operational once Kaseya has determined that we can safely restore operations. <u>We are in the process of formulating a staged return to service of our SaaS server farms with restricted functionality and a higher security posture (estimated in the next 24-48 hours but that is subject to change) on a geographic basis. More details on both the limitations, security posture changes, and time frame will be in the next communique later today.</u></li><li>All on-premises VSA Servers should continue to remain offline until further instructions from Kaseya about when it is safe to restore operations. A patch will be required to be installed prior to restarting the VSA <u>and a set of recommendations on how to increase security posture.</u></li><li><b>We have been advised by our outside experts, thatcustomers whoexperienced ransomware andreceive communication from the attackersshouldnot click onanylinksastheymay be weaponized.</b></li></ul><p><b><u>Key Points on Current Status</u></b></p><ul><li><u>The new Compromise Detection Tool was rolled out last night to almost 900 customers who requested the tool. Based on feedback from customers, we will be publishing an update to the tool this morning that improves its performance and usability. <b>There are no changes that will require a re-run of the tool on systems that have been scanned. </b><br /> This new version of the Compromise Detection Tool will be automatically sent to customers who received the first version. New requests can be made by sending an email to <a href="/cdn-cgi/l/email-protection#ccecbfb9bcbca3beb88ca7adbfa9b5ade2afa3a1"><span class="__cf_email__" data-cfemail="c6b5b3b6b6a9b4b286ada7b5a3bfa7e8a5a9ab">[email&#160;protected]</span></a> with the subject Compromise Detection Tool Request.</u></li><li><u>We will be opening up a private download site for end customers to get access to the Compromise Detection Tool once we have ensured the security, integrity, and trackability of the download process. More about this in the next update.</u></li><li>We continue to work with FireEye Mandiant IR (a leading computer incident response firm) on the security incident. <u>Our joint efforts have not identified any new IoCs since yesterday and we have deployed our Compromise Detection Tool at hundreds of customers. At this point, no False Positives have been reported by users. [Note: A False Positive indicates that the Compromise Detection Tool incorrectly classifies a system as impacted when it wasnt]</u></li><li>We have been actively engaged with <u>FireEye</u> and <u>other security assessment firms</u> to assess the manner and impact of the attack to ensure that our R&amp;D organization has properly identified and mitigated the vulnerability. We are continuing the investigation in parallel with the remediation steps.</li><li><u>R&amp;D has replicated the attack vector and the mitigation work is in progress. We expect to complete the work in the next 24-48 hours and the testing is progressing in parallel.</u></li><li><u>Fred Voccola, CEO of Kaseya, was interviewed regarding this incident on Good Morning America on the ABC network on Sunday, July 4th. The interview was significantly edited down from the full interview that Fred gave. The short message was: We are sure we know how it happened and we are remediating it.</u></li><li><u>We have engaged with the FBI and DHS CISA and are working with them on an incident-handling process for our worldwide customers impacted by the cyberattack. The following message will be posted to the FBI website:<br /> &#8220;If you feel your systems have been compromised as a result of the Kaseya ransomware incident,we encourage you to employ all recommended mitigations, follow Kaseya&#8217;s guidance to shut down your VSA servers immediately, and report your compromise to the FBI athttps://www.IC3.gov. Due to the potential scale of this incident, we may be unable to respond to each victim individually but all information we receive will be useful in countering this threat.</u></li><li>At this time, we believe that none of our NOC customers (neither SaaS nor on-premises) were affected by the attack. <u>Were continuing to investigate, but no compromised NOC customers have been found as of July 4th at 10:00 AM EDT.</u></li><li>Kaseya executives are directly reaching out to impacted customers to understand their situations and what assistance is possible. If you believe that you have been impacted, please contact <a href="/cdn-cgi/l/email-protection#3010434540405f4244705b51435549511e535f5d"><span class="__cf_email__" data-cfemail="6d1e181d1d021f192d060c1e08140c430e0200">[email&#160;protected]</span></a> with the subject Security Incident Report. <b><u>There have been no new reports of compromises since our last report yesterday.</u></b> We are confident we understand the scope of the issue and are partnering with each client to do everything possible to remediate. We believe that there is zero related risk right now for any VSA client who is a SaaS customer or on-premises VSA customer who has their server offline.</li></ul></div><h3 class="subtitle h3">July 3, 2021 - 9:00 PM EDT</h3><div class="description"><p>Kaseyas VSAproducthas unfortunatelybeenthe victim of a sophisticated cyberattack. Due to ourteamsfast response, we believe that this has been localized to a very small number of on-premisescustomersonly.</p><p>This update provides further detail on the 1:30 PM EDT update. <u>The changes are underlined for clarity.</u></p><p><b><u>Key Points on Current Status:</u></b></p><ul><li>All On-Premises VSA Servers should continue to remain offline until further instructions from Kaseya about when it is safe to restore operations. A patch will be required to be installed prior to restarting the VSA. We plan to give our first time estimate in tomorrow mornings update at approximately 9:00 AM EDT.</li><li>SaaS &amp; Hosted VSA Servers will become operational once Kaseya has determined that we can safely restore operations.</li><li><b>We have been advised by our outside experts, thatcustomers whoexperienced ransomware andreceive communication from the attackersshouldnot click onanylinks, astheymay be weaponized.</b></li><li><u>A Compromise Detection Tool will be available <b>later this evening</b> to Kaseya VSA customers by sending an email to <a href="/cdn-cgi/l/email-protection#bb9bc8cecbcbd4c9cffbd0dac8dec2da95d8d4d6"><span class="__cf_email__" data-cfemail="d0a3a5a0a0bfa2a490bbb1a3b5a9b1feb3bfbd">[email&#160;protected]</span></a> with the subject &#8220;Compromise Detection Tool Request&#8221; from an email address that is associated with a VSA customer.</u></li><li><u>With the availability of the Compromise Detection tool, we strongly recommend that compromised customers immediately begin the recovery process.</u></li><li><u>Fred Voccola, CEO of Kaseya, will be interviewed regarding this incident on Good Morning America on the ABC network on Sunday, July 4th. Please consult your local TV listings for times in your region. (This is subject to last minute rescheduling by the network)</u></li><li>Kaseya executives are directly reaching out to impacted customers to understand their situations and what assistance is possible. If you believe that you have been impacted, please contact <a href="/cdn-cgi/l/email-protection#0d2d7e787d7d627f794d666c7e68746c236e6260"><span class="__cf_email__" data-cfemail="cbb8bebbbba4b9bf8ba0aab8aeb2aae5a8a4a6">[email&#160;protected]</span></a> with the subject Security Incident Report. <u>There has been only one new report of a compromise occurring today due to a VSA on-premises server being left on. We are confident we understand the scope of the issue and are partnering with each client to do everything possible to remediate. We believe that there is zero related risk right now for any VSA client who is a SaaS customer or on-prem VSA customer who has their server off.</u></li><li>We have engaged a computer incident response firm (FireEye Mandiant IR) to identify the indicators of compromise (IoCs) to ensure that we can identify which systems and data were accessed. <u>We have identified a set of preliminary IoCs and have been working with our affected customers to validate them. The availability of the Compromise Detection Tool is based on our interactions with our outside experts.</u></li><li>We have been actively engaged with <u>FireEye</u> and <u>other security assessment firms</u> to assess the manner and impact of the attack to ensure that our R&amp;D organization has properly identified and mitigated the vulnerability.</li><li>R&amp;D has replicated the attack vector and is working on mitigating it. <u>We have begun the process of remediating the code and will include regular status updates on our progress starting tomorrow morning. We will begin working with select customers to field test the changes once we have completed the work and tested it thoroughly in our environment.</u> We will not publish a resolution timeframe until we have thoroughly validated and tested the proposed solution.</li><li>At this time, we believe that none of our NOC customers (neither SaaS nor on-premises) were affected by the attack. <u>Were continuing to investigate this, but no compromised NOC customers have been found as of 7:00 PM EDT.</u></li><li>We have engaged with the FBI and are working with them on an incident-handling process for our worldwide customers impacted by the cyberattack.</li></ul></div><h3 class="subtitle h3">July 3, 2021 - 1:30 PM EDT</h3><div class="description"><p>Kaseya is progressing on the security incident along multiple workstreams:</p><ul><li>Since the security of our customers is paramount, <b>we are continuing to strongly recommend that our on-premises customers VSA servers remain offline until further notice.</b> We will also keep our SaaS servers offline until further notice.</li><li><b>We have been advised by our outside experts, that customers who experienced ransomware and receive communication from the attackers should not click on any links &#8212; they may be weaponized.</b></li><li>We have engaged with the FBI and are working with them on an incident handling process for our worldwide customers impacted by the cyberattack. We will be publishing a list of contacts later today.</li><li>Kaseya executives are directly reaching out to impacted customers to understand their situations and what assistance is possible. Anyone who believes they have been impacted should contact <a href="/cdn-cgi/l/email-protection" class="__cf_email__" data-cfemail="9cefe9ececf3eee8dcf7fdeff9e5fdb2fff3f1">[email&#160;protected]</a> with the subject Security Incident Report.</li><li>We continue to engage with industry experts to assess the manner and impact of the attack and ensure that our R&amp;D organization has properly identified and mitigated the vulnerability.</li><li>R&amp;D has replicated the attack vector and is working on mitigating it. We will not publish a resolution timeframe until we have thoroughly validated and tested the proposed solution. We appreciate our customers patience.</li><li>We have engaged a computer forensics firm to identify the indicators of compromise (IOCs) to ensure that we can identify which systems and data were accessed.</li><li>R&amp;D is working on a self-assessment tool for our customers, to enable them to definitively determine whether they were affected. This will be published as part of the patch for on-premises customers.</li></ul><p>At this time, we believe that none of our NOC customers (neither SaaS nor on-premises) were affected by the attack. Were continuing to investigate this.</p><ul><li><b>ALL ON-PREMISES VSA SERVERS SHOULD CONTINUE TO REMAIN OFFLINE UNTIL FURTHER INSTRUCTIONS FROM KASEYA ABOUT WHEN IT IS SAFE TO RESTORE OPERATIONS. A PATCH WILL BE REQUIRED TO BE INSTALLED PRIOR TO RESTARTING THE VSA.</b></li><li><b>SAAS &amp; HOSTED VSA SERVERS WILL BECOME OPERATIONAL ONCE KASEYA HAS DETERMINED THAT WE CAN SAFELY RESTORE OPERATIONS.</b></li></ul></div><h3 class="subtitle h3">July 3, 2021 - 10:30 AM EDT</h3><div class="description"><p>Kaseyas VSAproducthas unfortunatelybeenthe victim of a sophisticated cyberattack.Due to ourteamsfast response, we believe that this has been localized to a very small number of on-premisescustomersonly.</p><p>Since the security of our customers is paramount,<strong>weare continuing to strongly recommend that our on-premisescustomers VSA servers remain down until further notice.</strong>We will also keep our SaaS servers offline until further notice.</p><p><strong>We have been advised by our outside experts, that customers whoexperienced ransomware andreceive a communication from the attackersshouldnot click onanylinks&#8211;theymay be weaponized.</strong></p><p>Kaseya has been workingaround the clockto resolvethis issue from asecurity assessment,client support, progress update, technical resolution, and return to operational status standpoint.</p><p>A comprehensive update is in progress and will be publishedlater thismorning(EDT). Thiscommunicationwill include prescriptive information on:</p><ul><li>The external authorities (FBI,Incident ResponseExperts) that we have engaged and how we are leveraging them for assistance;</li><li>Howour customers canengage Kaseya for assistanceand what we can do to help;</li><li>How to determine whether customershave beencompromised;</li><li>Status updates from R&amp;D on the progress of the patch for on-premisesusers;</li><li>Theplan to bring our SaaS andon-premisescustomers backonline;</li><li>A detailed description of theSecurity Incidentprocess andcurrent status;</li><li>A schedule for communications updates;</li><li>Other important information about therecovery process.</li></ul><p>Ongoing updates will be provided every 3-4 hours or more often based on breaking details.</p><ol><li>ALL ON-PREMISEsVSA SERVERS SHOULD CONTINUE TO REMAIN OFFLINE UNTIL FURTHER INSTRUCTIONS FROM KASEYA.</li><li>SAAS &amp; HOSTED VSA SERVERS WILL BECOME OPERATIONAL ONCE KASEYA HAS DETERMINED THAT WE CAN SAFELY RESTORE OPERATIONS.</li></ol></div><h3 class="subtitle h3">July 2, 2021 - 10:00 PM EDT</h3><div class="description"><p>Beginning around mid-day (EDT/US) on Friday July 2, 2021, Kaseyas Incident Response team learned of a potential security incident involving our VSA software.</p><p><strong>We took swift actions to protect our customers:</strong></p><ul><li>Immediately shut down our SaaS servers as a precautionary measure, even though we had not received any reports of compromise from any SaaS or hosted customers;</li><li>Immediately notified our on-premises customers via email, in-product notices, and phone to shut down their VSA servers to prevent them from being compromised.</li></ul><p>We then followed our established incident response process to determine the scope of the incident and the extent that our customers were affected.</p><ul><li>We engaged our internal incident response team and leading industry experts in forensic investigations to help us determine the root cause of the issue;</li><li>We notified law enforcement and government cybersecurity agencies, including the FBI and CISA.</li></ul><p>While our early indicators suggested that only a very small number of on-premises customers were affected, we took a conservative approach in shutting down the SaaS servers to ensure we protected our more than 36,000 customers to the best of our ability. We have received positive feedback from our customers on our rapid and proactive response.</p><p><strong>While our investigation is ongoing, to date we believe that:</strong></p><ul><li>Our SaaS customers were never at-risk. We expect to restore service to those customers once we have confirmed that they are not at risk, which we expect will be within the next 24 hours;</li><li>Only a very small percentage of our customers were affected  currently estimated at fewer than 40 worldwide.</li></ul><p>We believe that we have identified the source of the vulnerability and are preparing a patch to mitigate it for our on-premises customers that will be tested thoroughly. We will release that patch as quickly as possible to get our customers back up and running.</p><p>I am proud to report that our team had a plan in place to jump into action and executed that plan perfectly today. Weve heard from the vast majority of our customers that they experienced no issues at all, and I am grateful to our internal teams, outside experts, and industry partners who worked alongside of us to quickly bring this to a successful outcome.</p><p>Todays actions are a testament to Kaseyas unwavering commitment to put our customers first and provide the highest level of support for our products.</p><p>Fred Voccola, CEO<br /> Kaseya</p></div></div></div></div></div></section><section id="" class="border-top py-5"  ><div class="container"><div class="row justify-content-lg-center"><div class=" col-12 col-lg-10"><div class="custom"><h2 class="title display-4">Information Regarding Potential Attack on Kaseya VSA</h2><h3 class="subtitle h4">July 2, 2021 - 4:00 PM EST</h3><div class="description"><p>We are investigating a potential attack against the VSA that indicates to have been limited to a small number of our on-premises customers only. We have proactively shut down our SaaS servers out of an abundance of caution.</p><p><strong>We are in the process of investigating the root cause of the incident with the utmost vigilance, we have:</strong></p><ul><li>Notified all of our on-premise customers to immediately shutdown their VSA servers</li><li>Shutdown our SaaS Servers</li></ul><p>We have been further notified by a few security firms of the issue and we are working closely with them as well. While we continue to investigate the incident, we will update our customers (and interested parties) as we have more information.</p><p>Sincerely,<br /> Kaseya</p></div></div></div></div></div></section></main></div></div></div></div><footer class="main-footer bg-light" data-emergence="hidden"><div class="foot-wrap py-5"><div class="container"><div
